   More Info: https://bandit.readthedocs.io/en/latest/plugins/b824_url_found.html
220	            auth_method=AWSAuthenticationMethods.IMPLICIT,
221	            description="""
222	Implicit authentication to AWS services using environment variables, local
223	configuration files or IAM roles. This authentication method doesn't require
224	any credentials to be explicitly configured. It automatically discovers and uses
225	credentials from one of the following sources:
226	
227	- environment variables (AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID, AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY,
228	AWS_SESSION_TOKEN, AWS_DEFAULT_REGION)
229	- local configuration files [set up through the AWS CLI](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/cli/latest/userguide/cli-chap-configure.html)
230	(~/aws/credentials, ~/.aws/config)
231	- IAM roles for Amazon EC2, ECS, EKS, Lambda, etc. Only works when running
232	the ZenML server on an AWS resource with an IAM role attached to it.
233	
234	This is the quickest and easiest way to authenticate to AWS services. However,
235	the results depend on how ZenML is deployed and the environment where it is used
236	and is thus not fully reproducible:
237	
238	- when used with the default local ZenML deployment or a local ZenML server, the
239	credentials are the same as those used by the AWS CLI or extracted from local
240	environment variables.
241	- when connected to a ZenML server, this method only works if the ZenML server
242	is deployed in AWS and will use the IAM role attached to the AWS resource where
243	the ZenML server is running (e.g. an EKS cluster). The IAM role permissions may
244	need to be adjusted to allows listing and accessing/describing the AWS resources
245	that the connector is configured to access.
246	
247	An IAM role may optionally be specified to be assumed by the connector on top of
248	the implicit credentials. This is only possible when the implicit credentials
249	have permissions to assume the target IAM role. Configuring an IAM role has all
250	the advantages of the AWS IAM Role authentication method plus the added benefit
251	of not requiring any explicit credentials to be configured and stored:
252	
253	* The connector will generate temporary STS tokens upon request by
254	[calling the AssumeRole STS API](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/id_credentials_temp_request.html#api_assumerole).
255	* Allows implementing a two layer authentication scheme that keeps the set of
256	permissions associated with implicit credentials down to the bare minimum and
257	grants permissions to the privilege-bearing IAM role instead.
258	* One or more optional [IAM session policies](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/access_policies.html#policies_session)
259	may also be configured to further restrict the permissions of the generated
260	STS tokens. If not specified, IAM session policies are automatically configured
261	for the generated STS tokens to restrict them to the minimum set of permissions
262	required to access the target resource. Refer to the documentation for each
263	supported Resource Type for the complete list of AWS permissions automatically
264	granted to the generated STS tokens.
265	* The default expiration period for generated STS tokens is 1 hour with a
266	minimum of 15 minutes up to the maximum session duration setting configured for
267	the IAM role (default is 1 hour). If you need longer-lived tokens, you can
268	configure the IAM role to use a higher maximum expiration value (up to 12 hours)
269	or use the AWS Federation Token or AWS Session Token authentication methods.
270	
271	Note that the discovered credentials inherit the full set of permissions of the
272	local AWS client configuration, environment variables or attached AWS IAM role.
273	Depending on the extent of those permissions, this authentication method might
274	not be recommended for production use, as it can lead to accidental privilege
275	escalation. It is recommended to also configure an IAM role when using
276	the implicit authentication method, or to use the AWS IAM Role, AWS Session
277	Token or AWS Federation Token authentication methods instead to limit the
278	validity and/or permissions of the credentials being issued to connector
279	clients.
280	
281	If you need to access an EKS kubernetes cluster with this authentication method,
282	please be advised that the EKS cluster's aws-auth ConfigMap may need to be
283	manually configured to allow authentication with the implicit IAM user or role
284	picked up by the Service Connector. For more information,
285	[see this documentation](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/eks/latest/userguide/add-user-role.html).
286	
287	An AWS region is required and the connector may only be used to access AWS
288	resources in the specified region.
289	""",
290	            min_expiration_seconds=900,  # 15 minutes

396	AWS IAM Role authentication method and are more suitable for long-running

409	authentication method is automatically chosen instead of the AWS Secret Key
410	authentication method alternative.
411

413	AWS account root user that is calling the GetSessionToken API. Depending on your
414	security needs, this may not be suitable for production use, as it can lead to
415	accidental privilege escalation. Instead, it is recommended to use the AWS
416	Federation Token or AWS IAM Role authentication methods to restrict the

232	Implicit authentication to Azure services using environment variables, local
233	configuration files, workload or managed identities. This authentication method
234	doesn't require any credentials to be explicitly configured. It automatically
235	discovers and uses credentials from one of the following sources:
236	
237	- [environment variables](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/python/api/overview/azure/identity-readme?view=azure-python#environment-variables)
238	- workload identity - if the application is deployed to an Azure Kubernetes
239	Service with Managed Identity enabled. This option can only be used when running
240	the ZenML server on an AKS cluster.
241	- managed identity - if the application is deployed to an Azure host with
242	Managed Identity enabled. This option can only be used when running the ZenML client or server on
243	an Azure host.
244	- Azure CLI - if a user has signed in via [the Azure CLI `az login` command](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/cli/azure/authenticate-azure-cli).
245	
246	This is the quickest and easiest way to authenticate to Azure services. However,
247	the results depend on how ZenML is deployed and the environment where it is used
248	and is thus not fully reproducible:
249	
250	- when used with the default local ZenML deployment or a local ZenML server, the
251	credentials are the same as those used by the Azure CLI or extracted from local
252	environment variables.
253	- when connected to a ZenML server, this method only works if the ZenML server
254	is deployed in Azure and will use the workload identity attached to the Azure
255	resource where the ZenML server is running (e.g. an AKS cluster). The
256	permissions of the managed identity may need to be adjusted to allow listing
257	and accessing/describing the Azure resources that the connector is configured to
258	access.
259	
260	Note that the discovered credentials inherit the full set of permissions of the
261	local Azure CLI configuration, environment variables or remote Azure managed
262	identity. Depending on the extent of those permissions, this authentication
263	method might not be recommended for production use, as it can lead to accidental
264	privilege escalation. Instead, it is recommended to use the Azure service
265	principal authentication method to limit the validity and/or permissions of the
266	credentials being issued to connector clients.
267	""",

670	The ZenML GCP Service Connector facilitates the authentication and access to
671	managed GCP services and resources. These encompass a range of resources,
672	including GCS buckets, GCR container repositories and GKE clusters. The
673	connector provides support for various authentication methods, including GCP
674	user accounts, service accounts, short-lived OAuth 2.0 tokens and implicit
675	authentication.
676	
677	To ensure heightened security measures, this connector always issues short-lived
678	OAuth 2.0 tokens to clients instead of long-lived credentials unless explicitly
679	configured to do otherwise. Furthermore, it includes automatic configuration and
680	detection of credentials locally configured through the GCP CLI.
681	
682	This connector serves as a general means of accessing any GCP service by issuing
683	OAuth 2.0 credential objects to clients. Additionally, the connector can handle
684	specialized authentication for GCS, Docker and Kubernetes Python clients. It
685	also allows for the configuration of local Docker and Kubernetes CLIs.
686	
687	The GCP Service Connector is part of the GCP ZenML integration. You can either
688	install the entire integration or use a pypi extra to install it independently
689	of the integration:
690	
691	* `pip install "zenml[connectors-gcp]"` installs only prerequisites for the GCP
692	Service Connector Type
693	* `zenml integration install gcp` installs the entire GCP ZenML integration
694	
695	It is not required to install and set up [the GCP CLI](https://cloud.google.com/sdk/gcloud)
696	on your local machine to use the GCP Service Connector to link Stack Components
697	to GCP resources and services. However, it is recommended to do so if you are
698	looking for a quick setup that includes using the auto-configuration Service
699	Connector features.
700	""",

   More Info: https://bandit.readthedocs.io/en/latest/plugins/b824_url_found.html
707	            auth_method=GCPAuthenticationMethods.IMPLICIT,
708	            description="""
709	Implicit authentication to GCP services using [Application Default Credentials](https://cloud.google.com/docs/authentication/provide-credentials-adc).
710	This authentication method doesn't require any credentials to be explicitly
711	configured. It automatically discovers and uses credentials from one of the
712	following sources:
713	
714	- environment variables (`GOOGLE_APPLICATION_CREDENTIALS`)
715	- local ADC credential files set up by running `gcloud auth application-default
716	login` (e.g. `~/.config/gcloud/application_default_credentials.json`).
717	- GCP service account attached to the resource where the ZenML server is running.
718	Only works when running the ZenML server on a GCP resource with an service
719	account attached to it or when using Workload Identity (e.g. GKE cluster).
720	
721	This is the quickest and easiest way to authenticate to GCP services. However,
722	the results depend on how ZenML is deployed and the environment where it is used
723	and is thus not fully reproducible:
724	
725	- when used with the default local ZenML deployment or a local ZenML server, the
726	credentials are those set up on your machine (i.e. by running
727	`gcloud auth application-default login` or setting the
728	`GOOGLE_APPLICATION_CREDENTIALS` environment variable to point to a service
729	account key JSON file).
730	- when connected to a ZenML server, this method only works if the ZenML server
731	is deployed in GCP and will use the service account attached to the GCP resource
732	where the ZenML server is running (e.g. an GKE cluster). The service account
733	permissions may need to be adjusted to allow listing and accessing/describing
734	the GCP resources that the connector is configured to access.
735	
736	Note that the discovered credentials inherit the full set of permissions of the
737	local GCP CLI credentials or service account attached to the ZenML server GCP
738	workload. Depending on the extent of those permissions, this authentication
739	method might not be suitable for production use, as it can lead to accidental
740	privilege escalation. Instead, it is recommended to use the Service Account Key
741	or Service Account Impersonation authentication methods to restrict the
742	permissions that are granted to the connector clients.
743	
744	To find out more about Application Default Credentials,
745	[see the GCP ADC documentation](https://cloud.google.com/docs/authentication/provide-credentials-adc).
746	
747	A GCP project is required and the connector may only be used to access GCP
748	resources in the specified project. When used remotely in a GCP workload, the
749	configured project has to be the same as the project of the attached service
750	account.
751	""",
752	            config_class=GCPBaseProjectIDConfig,

1011	- `artifactregistry.repositories.list`
1012	- `artifactregistry.repositories.readViaVirtualRepository`
1013	- `artifactregistry.repositories.uploadArtifacts`
1014	- `artifactregistry.locations.list`
1015	
1016	The Artifact Registry Create-on-Push Writer role includes all of the above
1017	permissions.
1018	
1019	This resource type also includes legacy GCR container registry support.
1020	
1021	**Important Notice: Google Container Registry** [**is being replaced by Artifact Registry**](https://cloud.google.com/artifact-registry/docs/transition/transition-from-gcr).
1022	Please start using Artifact Registry for your containers. As per Google's
1023	documentation, *"after May 15, 2024, Artifact Registry will host images for the
1024	gcr.io domain in Google Cloud projects without previous Container Registry
1025	usage. After March 18, 2025, Container Registry will be shut down."*.
1026	
1027	Support for legacy GCR registries is still included in the GCP service
1028	connector. Users that already have GCP service connectors configured to access
1029	GCR registries may continue to use them without taking any action. However, it
1030	is recommended to transition to Google Artifact Registries as soon as possible
1031	by following [the GCP guide on this subject](https://cloud.google.com/artifact-registry/docs/transition/transition-from-gcr)
1032	and making the following updates to ZenML GCP Service Connectors that are used
1033	to access GCR resources:
1034	
1035	* add the IAM permissions documented here to the GCP Service Connector
1036	credentials to enable them to access the Artifact Registries.
1037	* users may keep the gcr.io GCR URLs already configured in the GCP Service
1038	Connectors as well as those used in linked Container Registry stack components
1039	given that these domains are redirected by Google to GAR as covered in the GCR
1040	transition guide. Alternatively, users may update the GCP Service Connector
1041	configuration and/or the Container Registry stack components to use the
1042	replacement Artifact Registry URLs.
1043	
1044	When used with GCR registries, the configured credentials must have at least the
1045	following [GCP permissions](https://cloud.google.com/iam/docs/understanding-roles#cloud-storage-roles):
1046	
1047	- `storage.buckets.get`
1048	- `storage.multipartUploads.abort`
1049	- `storage.multipartUploads.create`
1050	- `storage.multipartUploads.list`
1051	- `storage.multipartUploads.listParts`
1052	- `storage.objects.create`
1053	- `storage.objects.delete`
1054	- `storage.objects.list`
1055	
1056	The Storage Legacy Bucket Writer role includes all of the above permissions
1057	while at the same time restricting access to only the GCR buckets.
1058	
1059	If set, the resource name must identify a GAR or GCR registry using one of the
1060	following formats:
1061	
1062	- Google Artifact Registry repository URI: `[https://]<region>-docker.pkg.dev/<project-id>/<registry-id>[/<repository-name>]`
1063	- Google Artifact Registry name: `projects/<project-id>/locations/<location>/repositories/<repository-id>`
1064	- (legacy) GCR repository URI: `[https://][us.|eu.|asia.]gcr.io/<project-id>[/<repository-name>]`
1065	
1066	The connector can only be used to access GAR and GCR registries in the GCP
1067	project that it is configured to use.
1068	""",
